<p><b>Ankara</b> (<small>English</small> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="/ŋ/ 'ng' in 'sing'">ŋ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> <small>Turkish</small> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Turkic_dialects" title="Help:IPA for Turkic dialects">[ˈaŋ.ka.ɾa]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata"> (<a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_pronunciation.ogg" title="File:Ankara pronunciation.ogg"><img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/></a> <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a5/Ankara_pronunciation.ogg" title="Ankara pronunciation.ogg">listen</a>)</small>), formerly known as <b>Ancyra</b> and <b>Angora</b>, is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_national_capitals" title="List of national capitals">capital</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a>. With a population of 4,587,558 in the urban center <small>(2014)</small> and 5,150,072 in <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Province" title="Ankara Province">its province</a> <small>(2015)</small>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citypopulation1_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-citypopulation1-1">[1]</a></sup> it is Turkey's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_largest_cities_and_second_largest_cities_by_country" title="List of largest cities and second largest cities by country">second largest</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Turkey" title="List of cities in Turkey">city</a> after <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>.</p>
<p>Ankara was <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Atatürk</a>'s headquarters from 1920 and has been the capital of the Republic since its founding in 1923, replacing Istanbul following the <a href="/wiki/Defeat_and_dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Defeat and dissolution of the Ottoman Empire">fall of the Ottoman Empire</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Turkey" title="Government of Turkey">government</a> is a prominent employer, but Ankara is also an important commercial and industrial city, located at the center of Turkey's road and railway networks. The city gave its name to the <a href="/wiki/Angora_wool" title="Angora wool">Angora wool</a> shorn from <a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbits</a>, the long-haired <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a> (the source of <a href="/wiki/Mohair" title="Mohair">mohair</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Angora" title="Turkish Angora">Angora cat</a>. The area is also known for its pears, honey, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscat_(grape_and_wine)" title="Muscat (grape and wine)">muscat</a> grapes. Although situated in one of the driest places of Turkey and surrounded mostly by steppe vegetation except for the forested areas on the southern periphery, Ankara can be considered a green city in terms of green areas per inhabitant, at 72 square metres (775 square feet) per head.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ankara is a very old city with various <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">Phrygian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">Hellenistic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_site" title="Archaeological site">archaeological sites</a>. The historical center of town is a rocky hill rising 150 m (500 ft) over the left bank of the Ankara Çayı, a tributary of the <a href="/wiki/Sakarya_River" title="Sakarya River">Sakarya River</a>, the classical Sangarius. The hill remains crowned by the ruins of the old citadel. Although few of its outworks have survived, there are well-preserved examples of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_architecture" title="Roman architecture">Roman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_architecture" title="Ottoman architecture">Ottoman architecture</a> throughout the city, the most remarkable being the 20 <span class="smallcaps"><span style="font-variant: small-caps; text-transform: lowercase;">BC</span></span> <a href="/wiki/Augusteum" title="Augusteum">Temple of Augustus and Rome</a> that boasts the <a href="/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum" title="Monumentum Ancyranum">Monumentum Ancyranum</a>, the inscription recording the <i><a href="/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti" title="Res Gestae Divi Augusti">Res Gestae Divi Augusti</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341-4">[4]</a></sup></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As with many ancient cities, Ankara has gone by several names over the ages. It has been identified with the <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittite</a> cult center <b>Ankuwaš</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qgmpff_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-qgmpff-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-xtxpyw_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-xtxpyw-6">[6]</a></sup> although this remains a matter of debate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gorny_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gorny-7">[7]</a></sup> In classical antiquity and during the medieval period, the city was known as <b>Ánkyra</b> (<span lang="grc">Ἄγκυρα</span>, <small><abbr title="literally">lit</abbr></small> "<a href="/wiki/Anchor" title="Anchor">anchor</a>") in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">Greek</a> and <b>Ancyra</b> in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Galatian_language" title="Galatian language">Galatian Celtic</a> name was probably a similar variant. Following its annexation by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seljuk_Turks" title="Seljuk Turks">Seljuk Turks</a> in 1073, the city became known in many European languages as <b>Angora</b>; it was also known in <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman Turkish</a> as <b>Engürü</b>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341-4">[4]</a></sup> The form "Angora" is preserved in the names of breeds of many different kinds of animals, and in the names of several locations in the US (see <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Angora_(disambiguation)" title="Angora (disambiguation)">Angora</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Ankara" title="History of Ankara">History of Ankara</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Ankara" title="Timeline of Ankara">Timeline of Ankara</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg/220px-MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg/330px-MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg/440px-MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MuseumOfAnatolianCivilizationsHittiteArtifacts.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alaca_H%C3%B6y%C3%BCk_bronze_standards" title="Alaca Höyük bronze standards">Alaca Höyük bronze standard</a> on display at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Anatolian_Civilizations" title="Museum of Anatolian Civilizations">Museum of Anatolian Civilizations</a>, Ankara.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The region's history can be traced back to the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Hattians" title="Hattians">Hattic</a> <a href="/wiki/Hattic_language" title="Hattic language">civilization</a>, which was succeeded in the 2nd millennium BC by the <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittites</a>, in the 10th century BC by the <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">Phrygians</a>, and later by the <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galatia" title="Galatia">Galatians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantines</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">Turks</a> (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Seljuq_Empire" title="Great Seljuq Empire">Seljuk</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_R%C3%BBm" title="Sultanate of Rûm">Sultanate of Rûm</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancient_history">Ancient history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ancient history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The oldest settlements in and around the city center of Ankara belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Hattians" title="Hattians">Hattic</a> <a href="/wiki/Hattic_language" title="Hattic language">civilization</a> which existed during the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> and was gradually absorbed c. 2000–1700 BC by the <a href="/wiki/Hittite_language" title="Hittite language">Indo-European</a> <a href="/wiki/Hittites" title="Hittites">Hittites</a>. The city grew significantly in size and importance under the <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">Phrygians</a> starting around 1000 BC, and experienced a large expansion following the mass migration from <a href="/wiki/Gordium" title="Gordium">Gordion</a>, (the capital of <a href="/wiki/Phrygia" title="Phrygia">Phrygia</a>), after an earthquake which severely damaged that city around that time. In Phrygian tradition, King <a href="/wiki/Midas" title="Midas">Midas</a> was venerated as the founder of Ancyra, but <a href="/wiki/Pausanias_(geographer)" title="Pausanias (geographer)">Pausanias</a> mentions that the city was actually far older, which accords with present archaeological knowledge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>Phrygian rule was succeeded first by <a href="/wiki/Lydia" title="Lydia">Lydian</a> and later by <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Persian</a> rule, though the strongly Phrygian character of the peasantry remained, as evidenced by the gravestones of the much later Roman period. Persian sovereignty lasted until the Persians' defeat at the hands of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_the_Great" title="Alexander the Great">Alexander the Great</a> who conquered the city in 333 BC. Alexander came from <a href="/wiki/Gordium" title="Gordium">Gordion</a> to Ankara and stayed in the city for a short period. After his death at <a href="/wiki/Babylon" title="Babylon">Babylon</a> in 323 BC and the subsequent division of his empire among his generals, Ankara and its environs fell into the share of <a href="/wiki/Antigonus_I_Monophthalmus" title="Antigonus I Monophthalmus">Antigonus</a>.</p>
<p>Another important expansion took place under the Greeks of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontus" title="Pontus">Pontos</a> who came there around 300 BC and developed the city as a trading center for the commerce of goods between the <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">Black Sea</a> ports and Crimea to the north; Assyria, Cyprus, and Lebanon to the south; and Georgia, Armenia and Persia to the east. By that time the city also took its name <i>Ἄγκυρα</i> (<i>Ánkyra</i>, meaning <i><a href="/wiki/Anchor" title="Anchor">anchor</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">ancient Greek</a>) which, in slightly modified form, provides the modern name of <i>Ankara</i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Celtic_history">Celtic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Celtic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dying_gaul.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1186" data-file-width="1458" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Dying_gaul.jpg/220px-Dying_gaul.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Dying_gaul.jpg/330px-Dying_gaul.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Dying_gaul.jpg/440px-Dying_gaul.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dying_gaul.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dying_Galatian" title="Dying Galatian">Dying Galatian</a></i> was a famous statue commissioned some time between 230–220 BC by King <a href="/wiki/Attalus_I" title="Attalus I">Attalos I</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pergamon" title="Pergamon">Pergamon</a> to honor his victory over the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Galatia" title="Galatia">Galatians</a> in <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>. Roman marble copy of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hellenistic_civilization" title="Hellenistic civilization">Hellenistic</a> work of the late 3rd century BC, at the <a href="/wiki/Capitoline_Museums" title="Capitoline Museums">Capitoline Museums</a>, Rome.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 278 BC, the city, along with the rest of central Anatolia, was occupied by a <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> group, the <a href="/wiki/Galatia" title="Galatia">Galatians</a>, who were the first to make Ankara one of their main tribal centers, the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Tectosages" title="Tectosages">Tectosages</a> tribe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> Other centers were <a href="/wiki/Pessinus" title="Pessinus">Pessinos</a>, today's <i>Balhisar</i>, for the <a href="/wiki/Trocmi" title="Trocmi">Trocmi</a> tribe, and <a href="/wiki/Tavium" title="Tavium">Tavium</a>, to the east of Ankara, for the <i>Tolstibogii</i> tribe. The city was then known as <i>Ancyra</i>. The Celtic element was probably relatively small in numbers; a warrior aristocracy which ruled over Phrygian-speaking peasants. However, the Celtic language continued to be spoken in Galatia for many centuries. At the end of the 4th century, <a href="/wiki/Jerome" title="Jerome">St. Jerome</a>, a native of Dalmatia, observed that the language spoken around Ankara was very similar to that being spoken in the northwest of the Roman world near <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">Trier</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_history">Roman history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Roman history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galatia_Map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="310" data-file-width="435" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Galatia_Map.png/260px-Galatia_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Galatia_Map.png/390px-Galatia_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/81/Galatia_Map.png 2x" width="260"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galatia_Map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ancyra was the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">Celtic</a> kingdom of <a href="/wiki/Galatia" title="Galatia">Galatia</a>, and later of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> province with the same name, after its conquest by <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> in 25 BC.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city was subsequently conquered by <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a> in 25 BC and passed under the control of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman Empire</a>. Now the capital city of the Roman province of Galatia, Ancyra continued to be a center of great commercial importance. Ankara is also famous for the <i><a href="/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum" title="Monumentum Ancyranum">Monumentum Ancyranum</a></i> (<i>Temple of Augustus and Rome</i>) which contains the official record of the <i>Acts of Augustus</i>, known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti" title="Res Gestae Divi Augusti">Res Gestae Divi Augusti</a></i>, an inscription cut in marble on the walls of this temple. The ruins of Ancyra still furnish today valuable <a href="/wiki/Relief" title="Relief">bas-reliefs</a>, inscriptions and other architectural fragments.</p>
<p>Augustus decided to make Ancyra one of three main administrative centers in central Anatolia. The town was then populated by Phrygians and Celts—the <i>Galatians</i> who spoke a language somewhat closely related to <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goidelic_languages" title="Goidelic languages">Gaelic</a>. Ancyra was the center of a tribe known as the <i>Tectosages</i>, and Augustus upgraded it into a major provincial capital for his empire. Two other Galatian tribal centers, <a href="/wiki/Tavium" title="Tavium">Tavium</a> near <a href="/wiki/Yozgat" title="Yozgat">Yozgat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pessinus" title="Pessinus">Pessinus</a> (Balhisar) to the west, near Sivrihisar, continued to be reasonably important settlements in the Roman period, but it was Ancyra that grew into a grand metropolis.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Res_Gestae.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1914" data-file-width="1272" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Res_Gestae.jpg/220px-Res_Gestae.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Res_Gestae.jpg/330px-Res_Gestae.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Res_Gestae.jpg/440px-Res_Gestae.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Res_Gestae.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Res_Gestae_Divi_Augusti" title="Res Gestae Divi Augusti">Res Gestae</a> is the self-laudatory autobiography completed in 13 AD, just before his death, by the first <a href="/wiki/Roman_emperor" title="Roman emperor">Roman emperor</a> <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">Augustus</a>. Most of the text is preserved in the <a href="/wiki/Monumentum_Ancyranum" title="Monumentum Ancyranum">Monumentum Ancyranum</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="604" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg/220px-AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg/330px-AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg/440px-AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AnkaraRomanBaths1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Baths_of_Ankara" title="Roman Baths of Ankara">Roman Baths of Ankara</a> were constructed by the Roman emperor <a href="/wiki/Caracalla" title="Caracalla">Caracalla</a> (212–217) in honor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asclepios" title="Asclepios">Asclepios</a>, the God of Medicine, and built around three principal rooms: the <i><a href="/wiki/Caldarium" title="Caldarium">caldarium</a></i> (hot bath), the <i><a href="/wiki/Tepidarium" title="Tepidarium">tepidarium</a></i> (warm bath) and the <i><a href="/wiki/Frigidarium" title="Frigidarium">frigidarium</a></i> (cold bath) in a typically laid-out 80-by-120-metre (260-by-390-foot) classical complex.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>An estimated 200,000 people lived in Ancyra in good times during the Roman Empire, a far greater number than was to be the case from after the fall of the Roman Empire until the early 20th century. A small river, the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_River" title="Ankara River">Ankara Çayı</a>, ran through the center of the Roman town. It has now been covered and diverted, but it formed the northern boundary of the old town during the Roman, Byzantine and Ottoman periods. Çankaya, the rim of the majestic hill to the south of the present city center, stood well outside the Roman city, but may have been a summer resort. In the 19th century, the remains of at least one <a href="/wiki/Roman_villa" title="Roman villa">Roman villa</a> or large house were still standing not far from where the Çankaya Presidential Residence stands today. To the west, the Roman city extended until the area of the Gençlik Park and Railway Station, while on the southern side of the hill, it may have extended downwards as far as the site presently occupied by <a href="/wiki/Hacettepe_University" title="Hacettepe University">Hacettepe University</a>. It was thus a sizeable city by any standards and much larger than the Roman towns of <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">Gaul</a> or <a href="/wiki/Britannia" title="Britannia">Britannia</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Ancyra's importance rested on the fact that it was the junction point where the roads in northern Anatolia running north-south and east-west intersected. The great imperial road running east passed through Ankara and a succession of emperors and their armies came this way. They were not the only ones to use the Roman highway network, which was equally convenient for invaders. In the second half of the 3rd century, Ancyra was invaded in rapid succession by the <a href="/wiki/Goths" title="Goths">Goths</a> coming from the west (who rode far into the heart of <a href="/wiki/Cappadocia" title="Cappadocia">Cappadocia</a>, taking slaves and pillaging) and later by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arab_people" title="Arab people">Arabs</a>. For about a decade, the town was one of the western outposts of one of Palmyrean empress <a href="/wiki/Zenobia" title="Zenobia">Zenobia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Desert" title="Syrian Desert">Syrian Desert</a>, who took advantage of a period of weakness and disorder in the Roman Empire to set up a short-lived state of her own.</p>
<p>The town was reincorporated into the Roman Empire under Emperor <a href="/wiki/Aurelian" title="Aurelian">Aurelian</a> in 272. The <a href="/wiki/Tetrarchy" title="Tetrarchy">tetrarchy</a>, a system of multiple (up to four) emperors introduced by <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">Diocletian</a> (284–305), seems to have engaged in a substantial programme of rebuilding and of road construction from Ankara westwards to Germe and <a href="/wiki/Dorylaeum" title="Dorylaeum">Dorylaeum</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Eski%C5%9Fehir" title="Eskişehir">Eskişehir</a>).</p>
<p>In its heyday, Roman Ankara was a large market and trading center but it also functioned as a major administrative capital, where a high official ruled from the city's Praetorium, a large administrative palace or office. During the 3rd century, life in Ancyra, as in other Anatolian towns, seems to have become somewhat militarized in response to the invasions and instability of the town.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christianity">Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Early Christian martyrs of Ancyra, about whom little is known, included Proklos and Hilarios who were natives of the otherwise unknown nearby village of Kallippi, and suffered repression under the emperor <a href="/wiki/Trajan" title="Trajan">Trajan</a> (98–117). In the 280s we hear of Philumenos, a Christian corn merchant from southern Anatolia, being captured and martyred in Ankara, and Eustathius.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teodot_Ankirski.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="426" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Teodot_Ankirski.jpg/170px-Teodot_Ankirski.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Teodot_Ankirski.jpg/255px-Teodot_Ankirski.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Teodot_Ankirski.jpg/340px-Teodot_Ankirski.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teodot_Ankirski.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Theodotus_of_Ancyra_(martyr)" title="Theodotus of Ancyra (martyr)">St. Theodotus of Ancyra</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>As in other Roman towns, the reign of <a href="/wiki/Diocletian" title="Diocletian">Diocletian</a> marked the culmination of the persecution of the Christians. In 303, Ancyra was one of the towns where the co-Emperors Diocletian and his deputy <a href="/wiki/Galerius" title="Galerius">Galerius</a> launched their anti-Christian persecution. In Ancyra, their first target was the 38-year-old Bishop of the town, whose name was Clement. Clement's life describes how he was taken to Rome, then sent back, and forced to undergo many interrogations and hardship before he, and his brother, and various companions were put to death. The remains of the church of <a href="/wiki/Clement_of_Ancyra" title="Clement of Ancyra">St. Clement</a> can be found today in a building just off Işıklar Caddesi in the Ulus district. Quite possibly this marks the site where Clement was originally buried. Four years later, a doctor of the town named Plato and his brother Antiochus also became celebrated martyrs under Galerius. <a href="/wiki/Theodotus_of_Ancyra_(martyr)" title="Theodotus of Ancyra (martyr)">Theodotus of Ancyra</a> is also venerated as a saint.</p>
<p>However, the persecution proved unsuccessful and in 314 Ancyra was the center of <a href="/wiki/Synod_of_Ancyra" title="Synod of Ancyra">an important council</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Early_Christianity" title="Early Christianity">early church</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERockwell1911_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockwell1911-11">[11]</a></sup> which considered ecclesiastical policy for the reconstruction of the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Church" title="Christian Church">Christian Church</a> after the persecutions, and in particular the treatment of 'lapsi'—Christians who had given in and conformed to <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">paganism</a> during these persecutions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERockwell1911_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockwell1911-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="1382" height="319" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG/170px-AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG/255px-AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG/340px-AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AnkaraColumnFar_c.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Column of Julian</i> (362) was erected in honor of the Roman emperor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate">Julian the Apostate</a>'s visit to Ancyra.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three councils were held in the former capital of Galatia in Asia Minor, during the 4th century. The first of these, the <a href="/wiki/Synod_of_Ancyra" title="Synod of Ancyra">Synod of Ancyra</a>, an orthodox plenary synod, was held in 314, and its 25 disciplinary canons constitute one of the most important documents in the early history of the administration of the <a href="/wiki/Confession_(religion)" title="Confession (religion)">Sacrament of Penance</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERockwell1911_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockwell1911-11">[11]</a></sup> Nine of them deal with conditions for the reconciliation of the lapsi; the others, with marriage, alienations of church property, etc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERockwell1911_11-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERockwell1911-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Though paganism was probably tottering in Ancyra in Clement's day, it may still have been the majority religion. Twenty years later, Christianity and <a href="/wiki/Monotheism" title="Monotheism">monotheism</a> had taken its place. Ancyra quickly turned into a Christian city, with a life dominated by monks and priests and theological disputes. The town council or senate gave way to the bishop as the main local figurehead. During the middle of the 4th century, Ancyra was involved in the complex theological disputes over the nature of Christ, and a form of <a href="/wiki/Arianism" title="Arianism">Arianism</a> seems to have originated there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEParvis2006325.E2.80.93345_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEParvis2006325.E2.80.93345-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 362–363, the Emperor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Julian_the_Apostate" title="Julian the Apostate">Julian the Apostate</a> passed through Ancyra on his way to an ill-fated campaign against the Persians, and according to Christian sources, engaged in a persecution of various holy men.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gibbon_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-gibbon-13">[13]</a></sup> The stone base for a statue, with an inscription describing Julian as "Lord of the whole world from the British Ocean to the barbarian nations", can still be seen, built into the eastern side of the inner circuit of the walls of Ankara Castle. The Column of Julian which was erected in honor of the emperor's visit to the city in 362 still stands today. In 375, Arian bishops met at Ancyra and deposed several bishops, among them <a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Nyssa" title="Gregory of Nyssa">St. Gregory of Nyssa</a>.</p>
<p>In the late 4th century, Ancyra became something of an imperial <a href="/wiki/Resort" title="Resort">holiday resort</a>. After <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> became the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">East Roman</a> capital, emperors in the 4th and 5th centuries would retire from the humid summer weather on the <a href="/wiki/Bosphorus" title="Bosphorus">Bosporus</a> to the drier mountain atmosphere of Ancyra. <a href="/wiki/Theodosius_II" title="Theodosius II">Theodosius II</a> (408–450) kept his court in Ancyra in the summers. Laws issued in Ancyra testify to the time they spent there. The city's military as well as logistical significance lasted well into the long <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine rule</a>. Although Ancyra temporarily fell into the hands of several Arab Muslim armies numerous times after the 7th century, it remained an important crossroads polis within the Byzantine Empire until the late 11th century. It was also the capital of the powerful <a href="/wiki/Opsikion" title="Opsikion">Opsician Theme</a>, and after c. 750 of the <a href="/wiki/Bucellarian_Theme" title="Bucellarian Theme">Bucellarian Theme</a>.</p>
<p>Ancyra, known in the West also as Angora, continued to be a residential <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_see" title="Episcopal see">see</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> until the 20th century, with about 40,000 faithful, mostly Turkish-speaking, but that situation ended as a result of the 1923 <a href="/wiki/Convention_Concerning_the_Exchange_of_Greek_and_Turkish_Populations" title="Convention Concerning the Exchange of Greek and Turkish Populations">Convention Concerning the Exchange of Greek and Turkish Populations</a>. The earlier <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Genocide" title="Armenian Genocide">Armenian Genocide</a> put an end to the residential eparchy of Ancyra of the <a href="/wiki/Armenian_Catholic_Church" title="Armenian Catholic Church">Armenian Catholic Church</a>, which had been established in 1850.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Both the Greek archbishopric and the Armenian eparchy are now listed by the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> as <a href="/wiki/Titular_see" title="Titular see">titular sees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> It is also a titular metropolis of the <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarchate_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarchate of Constantinople</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Turkish_history">Turkish history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Turkish history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2339" data-file-width="3303" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg/220px-Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg/330px-Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg/440px-Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atat%C3%BCrk_TBMM%27den_%C3%A7%C4%B1karken.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
President <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a> (center) and Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0smet_%C4%B0n%C3%B6n%C3%BC" title="İsmet İnönü">İsmet İnönü</a> (left) leaving the <a href="/wiki/Grand_National_Assembly_of_Turkey" title="Grand National Assembly of Turkey">Grand National Assembly of Turkey</a> during the 7th anniversary celebrations of the Turkish Republic in 1930.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Banks_Street_(Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard)_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_(Agricultural_Bank),_1930s_(16851406391).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1437" data-file-width="2000" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg/220px-Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg/330px-Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg/440px-Banks_Street_%28Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard%29_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_%28Agricultural_Bank%29%2C_1930s_%2816851406391%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Banks_Street_(Atat%C3%BCrk_Boulevard)_the_Building_of_Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1_(Agricultural_Bank),_1930s_(16851406391).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A view of the old general directorate building of <a href="/wiki/Ziraat_Bankas%C4%B1" title="Ziraat Bankası">Ziraat Bank</a>. It was designed by Istanbul-born <a href="/wiki/Levantines_(Latin_Christians)" title="Levantines (Latin Christians)">Italian Levantine</a> architect Giulio Mongeri and built between 1926 and 1929.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1071, the <a href="/wiki/Seljuq_dynasty" title="Seljuq dynasty">Seljuk Turkish</a> Sultan <a href="/wiki/Alp_Arslan" title="Alp Arslan">Alp Arslan</a> conquered much of <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">eastern and central Anatolia</a> after his victory at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manzikert" title="Battle of Manzikert">Battle of Manzikert</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Norwich241_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Norwich241-17">[17]</a></sup> He then annexed Ankara, an important location for military transportation and <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>, to his territory in 1073. In 1077 the Seljuk <a href="/wiki/Sultanate_of_Rum" title="Sultanate of Rum">Sultanate of Rum</a> (<a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a>) was established, which seceded from the greater <a href="/wiki/Seljuk_Empire" title="Seljuk Empire">Seljuk Empire</a>. The Byzantines recaptured Ankara in 1101. The <a href="/wiki/Danishmends" title="Danishmends">Danishmends</a> captured it in 1127. Finally, the Sultanate of Rum retook it in 1143. After the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_K%C3%B6se_Da%C4%9F" title="Battle of Köse Dağ">Battle of Köse Dağ</a> in 1243, in which the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_Empire" title="Mongol Empire">Mongols</a> defeated the Seljuks, most of Anatolia became part of the dominion of the Mongols. Taking advantage of Seljuk decline, a semi-religious cast of craftsmen and trade people named <i><a href="/wiki/Ahis" title="Ahis">Ahiler</a></i> chose Ankara as their independent city-state in 1290. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orhan_I" title="Orhan I">Orhan I</a>, the second <a href="/wiki/Bey" title="Bey">Bey</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>, captured the city in 1356. <a href="/wiki/Timur" title="Timur">Timur</a> defeated <a href="/wiki/Bayezid_I" title="Bayezid I">Bayezid I</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ankara" title="Battle of Ankara">Battle of Ankara</a> in 1402 and took the city, but in 1403 Ankara was again under Ottoman control.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Levant_Company" title="Levant Company">Levant Company</a> maintained a factory in the town from 1639 to 1768.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341-4">[4]</a></sup> In the 19th century, its population was estimated at 20,000 to 60,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845-8">[8]</a></sup> It was sacked by <a href="/wiki/Khedivate_of_Egypt" title="Khedivate of Egypt">Egyptians</a> under <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Pasha_of_Egypt" title="Ibrahim Pasha of Egypt">Ibrahim Pasha</a> in 1832.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341-4">[4]</a></sup> Prior to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the town had a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">consulate</a> and a population of around 28,000, roughly ⅓ of whom were Christian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_(2007-04-14)_edit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1469" data-file-width="2329" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_%282007-04-14%29_edit.jpg/220px-Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_%282007-04-14%29_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_%282007-04-14%29_edit.jpg/330px-Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_%282007-04-14%29_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_%282007-04-14%29_edit.jpg/440px-Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_%282007-04-14%29_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Protect_Your_Republic_Protest_-_6_(2007-04-14)_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/An%C4%B1tkabir" title="Anıtkabir">Anıtkabir</a>, the mausoleum of <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a> in Ankara, is visited by large crowds every year during national holidays such as Republic Day on October 29.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Su_perileri_ankara.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="471" data-file-width="800" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Su_perileri_ankara.jpg/220px-Su_perileri_ankara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Su_perileri_ankara.jpg/330px-Su_perileri_ankara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Su_perileri_ankara.jpg/440px-Su_perileri_ankara.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Su_perileri_ankara.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square" title="Kızılay Square">Kızılay Square</a> during the early years of the Turkish Republic, with the later relocated <i>Su Perileri</i> (Water Fairies) fountain, c. 1930.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gezenadam_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gezenadam-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SuPerileri_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-SuPerileri-19">[19]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> defeat at <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the Ottoman capital <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> (modern Istanbul) and much of <a href="/wiki/Anatolia" title="Anatolia">Anatolia</a> were occupied by the Allies, who planned to share these lands between <a href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_Armenia" title="First Republic of Armenia">Armenia</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Greece" title="Kingdom of Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Italy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>, leaving for the Turks the core piece of land in central Anatolia. In response, the leader of the Turkish nationalist movement, <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a>, established the headquarters of his <a href="/wiki/Turkish_National_Movement" title="Turkish National Movement">resistance movement</a> in Ankara in 1920. After the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_War_of_Independence" title="Turkish War of Independence">Turkish War of Independence</a> was won and the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_S%C3%A8vres" title="Treaty of Sèvres">Treaty of Sèvres</a> was superseded by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Lausanne" title="Treaty of Lausanne">Treaty of Lausanne</a>, the Turkish nationalists replaced the Ottoman Empire with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_Turkey" title="Republic of Turkey">Republic of Turkey</a> on 29 October 1923. A few days earlier, Ankara had officially replaced Constantinople as the new Turkish capital city, on 13 October 1923.</p>
<p>After Ankara became the capital of the newly founded Republic of Turkey, new development divided the city into an old section, called <i>Ulus</i>, and a new section, called <i>Yenişehir</i>. Ancient buildings reflecting Roman, Byzantine, and Ottoman history and narrow winding streets mark the old section. The new section, now centered on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Meydan%C4%B1" title="Kızılay Meydanı">Kızılay Square</a>, has the trappings of a more modern city: wide streets, hotels, theaters, shopping malls, and high-rises. Government offices and foreign embassies are also located in the new section. Ankara has experienced a phenomenal growth since it was made Turkey's capital in 1923, when it was "a small town of no importance".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In 1924, the year after the government had moved there, Ankara had about 35,000 residents. By 1927 there were 44,553 residents and by 1950 the population had grown to 286,781. Ankara continued to grow rapidly during the latter half of the 20th century and eventually outranked <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Izmir" title="Izmir">Izmir</a> as Turkey's second largest city, after <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>. Ankara's urban population reached 4,587,558 in 2014, while the population of <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Province" title="Ankara Province">Ankara Province</a> reached 5,150,072 in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-citypopulation1_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-citypopulation1-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1008px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG" title="A panoramic view of the city from the Ankara castle and citadel"><img alt="" data-file-height="897" data-file-width="3227" height="278" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG/1000px-Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG/1500px-Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG/2000px-Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG 2x" width="1000"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ankara_Kalesi%27nden_%C5%9Fehir_panoramas%C4%B1.JPG" title="File:Ankara Kalesi'nden şehir panoraması.JPG"></a></div>
<center>A panoramic view of the city from the <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Castle" title="Ankara Castle">Ankara castle and citadel</a></center>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ankara has a dry summer <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a> (<i>Dsa</i>) under the <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>, with some regions of the province having a warm summer subtype (<i>Dsb</i>) depending on elevation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Under the <a href="/wiki/Trewartha_climate_classification" title="Trewartha climate classification">Trewartha climate classification</a>, Ankara has a middle latitude steppe climate (<i>BSks</i>). Due to its elevation and inland location, Ankara has cold, snowy winters and hot, dry summers, with cool nightly temperatures. Rainfall occurs mostly during the spring and autumn. Ankara lies in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USDA" title="USDA">USDA</a> <a href="/wiki/Hardiness_zone" title="Hardiness zone">Hardiness zone</a> 7b, and its annual average precipitation is fairly low at 400 millimeters (16 in), nevertheless precipitation can be observed throughout the year. Monthly mean temperatures range from 0.3 °C (32.5 °F) in January to 23.5 °C (74.3 °F) in July, with an annual mean of 12.02 °C (53.6 °F).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ankara_road_map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="937" data-file-width="1122" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ankara_road_map.png/160px-Ankara_road_map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ankara_road_map.png/240px-Ankara_road_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Ankara_road_map.png/320px-Ankara_road_map.png 2x" width="160"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ankara_road_map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Ankara <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ankara had a population of 75,000 in 1927. In 2013, Ankara Province had a population of 5,045,083.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turkey_pop_2007_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Turkey_pop_2007-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Ankara became the capital of the Republic of Turkey in 1923, it was designated as a planned city for 500,000 future inhabitants. During the 1920s, 1930s and 1940s, the city grew in a planned and orderly pace. However, from the 1950s onward, the city grew much faster than envisioned, because unemployment and poverty forced people to migrate from the countryside into the city in order to seek a better standard of living. As a result, many illegal houses called <a href="/wiki/Gecekondu" title="Gecekondu">gecekondu</a> were built around the city, causing the unplanned and uncontrolled urban landscape of Ankara, as not enough planned housing could be built fast enough. Although precariously built, the vast majority of them have electricity, running water and modern household amenities.</p>
<p>Nevertheless, many of these gecekondus have been replaced by huge public housing projects in the form of <a href="/wiki/Tower_block" title="Tower block">tower blocks</a> such as Elvankent, <a href="/wiki/Eryaman,_Etimesgut" title="Eryaman, Etimesgut">Eryaman</a> and <a href="/wiki/G%C3%BCzelkent,_Etimesgut" title="Güzelkent, Etimesgut">Güzelkent</a>; and also as mass housing compounds for military and civil service accommodation. Although many gecekondus still remain, they too are gradually being replaced by mass housing compounds, as empty land plots in the city of Ankara for new construction projects are becoming impossible to find.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_view_of_the_BDDK_building,_Atat%C3%BCrk_Avenue_in_Ankara.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A_view_of_the_BDDK_building%2C_Atat%C3%BCrk_Avenue_in_Ankara.jpg/170px-A_view_of_the_BDDK_building%2C_Atat%C3%BCrk_Avenue_in_Ankara.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A_view_of_the_BDDK_building%2C_Atat%C3%BCrk_Avenue_in_Ankara.jpg/255px-A_view_of_the_BDDK_building%2C_Atat%C3%BCrk_Avenue_in_Ankara.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/A_view_of_the_BDDK_building%2C_Atat%C3%BCrk_Avenue_in_Ankara.jpg/340px-A_view_of_the_BDDK_building%2C_Atat%C3%BCrk_Avenue_in_Ankara.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>

BDDK Building (1975)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_in_Ankara,_Turkey.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_in_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG/300px-K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_in_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_in_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG/450px-K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_in_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_in_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG/600px-K%C4%B1z%C4%B1lay_Square_in_Ankara%2C_Turkey.JPG 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sogutozu_Ankara_Turkey.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="293" data-file-width="800" height="110" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sogutozu_Ankara_Turkey.jpg/300px-Sogutozu_Ankara_Turkey.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sogutozu_Ankara_Turkey.jpg/450px-Sogutozu_Ankara_Turkey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sogutozu_Ankara_Turkey.jpg/600px-Sogutozu_Ankara_Turkey.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6%C4%9F%C3%BCt%C3%B6z%C3%BC" title="Söğütözü">Söğütözü</a> business district in Ankara, as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Forest_Farm_and_Zoo" title="Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo">Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo</a>, with the Armada Tower &amp; Mall (2002) rising behind the Turkish flag.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city has exported <a href="/wiki/Mohair" title="Mohair">mohair</a> (from the <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Angora_wool" title="Angora wool">Angora wool</a> (from the <a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbit</a>) internationally for centuries. In the 19th century, the city also exported substantial amounts of <a href="/wiki/Goatskin_(material)" title="Goatskin (material)">goat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catskin" title="Catskin">cat skins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gum_arabic" title="Gum arabic">gum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beeswax" title="Beeswax">wax</a>, <a href="/wiki/Honey" title="Honey">honey</a>, berries, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madder_root" title="Madder root">madder root</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBaynes187845-8">[8]</a></sup> It was connected to <a href="/wiki/Constantinople" title="Constantinople">Constantinople</a> by railway before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_World_War" title="First World War">First World War</a>, continuing to export mohair, wool, berries, and <a href="/wiki/Grain" title="Grain">grain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEChisholm191140.E2.80.9341-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Anatolia_Region" title="Central Anatolia Region">Central Anatolia Region</a> is one of the primary locations of grape and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_wine" title="Turkish wine">wine production in Turkey</a>, and Ankara is particularly famous for its <a href="/wiki/Kalecik_Karas%C4%B1" title="Kalecik Karası">Kalecik Karası</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muscat_(grape_and_wine)" title="Muscat (grape and wine)">Muscat grapes</a>; and its <a href="/wiki/Kavakl%C4%B1dere_(winery)" title="Kavaklıdere (winery)">Kavaklıdere wine</a>, which is produced in the <a href="/wiki/Kavakl%C4%B1dere,_Ankara" title="Kavaklıdere, Ankara">Kavaklıdere</a> neighbourhood within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%87ankaya,_Ankara" title="Çankaya, Ankara">Çankaya</a> district of the city. Ankara is also famous for its pears. Another renowned natural product of Ankara is its indigenous type of <a href="/wiki/Honey" title="Honey">honey</a> (<i>Ankara Balı</i>) which is known for its light color and is mostly produced by the <a href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_Forest_Farm_and_Zoo" title="Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo">Atatürk Forest Farm and Zoo</a> in the Gazi district, and by other facilities in the Elmadağ, Çubuk and Beypazarı districts.</p>
<p>Ankara is the center of the state-owned and private Turkish <a href="/wiki/Arms_industry" title="Arms industry">defence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aerospace_manufacturer" title="Aerospace manufacturer">aerospace</a> companies, where the industrial plants and headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Aerospace_Industries" title="Turkish Aerospace Industries">Turkish Aerospace Industries</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanical_and_Chemical_Industry_Corporation_(Turkey)" title="Mechanical and Chemical Industry Corporation (Turkey)">MKE</a>, <a href="/wiki/ASELSAN" title="ASELSAN">ASELSAN</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Havelsan" title="Havelsan">Havelsan</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roketsan" title="Roketsan">Roketsan</a>, <a href="/wiki/FNSS_Defence_Systems" title="FNSS Defence Systems">FNSS</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nurol_Makina" title="Nurol Makina">Nurol Makina</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> and numerous other firms are located. Exports to foreign countries from these defence and aerospace firms have steadily increased in the past decades. The <a href="/wiki/International_Defence_Industry_Fair" title="International Defence Industry Fair">IDEF</a> in Ankara is one of the largest international expositions of the global <a href="/wiki/Arms_industry" title="Arms industry">arms industry</a>. A number of the global <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry" title="Automotive industry">automotive companies</a> also have production facilities in Ankara, such as the German bus and truck manufacturer <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">MAN SE</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> Ankara hosts the <a href="/wiki/OSTIM_Industrial_Zone" title="OSTIM Industrial Zone">OSTIM Industrial Zone</a>, Turkey's largest <a href="/wiki/Industrial_park" title="Industrial park">industrial park</a>.</p>
<p>A large percentage of the complicated employment in Ankara is provided by the state institutions; such as the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_(government_department)" title="Ministry (government department)">ministries</a>, undersecretariats, and other administrative bodies of the Turkish government. There are also many foreign citizens working as diplomats or clerks in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Embassy" title="Embassy">embassies</a> of their respective countries.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em">

<p>Ankara is politically a triple battleground between the ruling conservative <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">Justice and Development Party</a> (AKP), the opposition <a href="/wiki/Kemalism" title="Kemalism">Kemalist</a> centre-left <a href="/wiki/Republican_People%27s_Party_(Turkey)" title="Republican People's Party (Turkey)">Republican People's Party</a> (CHP) and the nationalist far-right <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Movement_Party" title="Nationalist Movement Party">Nationalist Movement Party</a> (MHP). The <a href="/wiki/Ankara_Province" title="Ankara Province">province of Ankara</a> is divided into 25 districts. The CHP's key and almost only political stronghold in Ankara lies within the central area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%87ankaya" title="Çankaya">Çankaya</a>, which is the city's most populous district. While the CHP has always gained between 60 and 70% of the vote in Çankaya since 2002, political support elsewhere throughout Ankara is minimal. The high population within Çankaya, as well as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yenimahalle" title="Yenimahalle">Yenimahalle</a> to an extent, has allowed the CHP to take overall second place behind the AKP in both local and general elections, with the MHP a close third, despite the fact that the MHP is politically stronger than the CHP in almost every other district. Overall, the AKP enjoys the most support throughout the city. The electorate of Ankara thus tend to vote in favour of the political right, far more so than the other main cities of <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a> and <a href="/wiki/%C4%B0zmir" title="İzmir">İzmir</a>. In retrospect, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_protests_in_Turkey" title="2013–14 protests in Turkey">2013–14 protests against the AKP government</a> were particularly strong in Ankara, proving to be fatal on multiple occasions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Melih_G%C3%B6k%C3%A7ek" title="Melih Gökçek">Melih Gökçek</a> has been the Metropolitan Mayor of Ankara since 1994 as a politician from the <a href="/wiki/Welfare_Party" title="Welfare Party">Welfare Party</a>. He later joined the <a href="/wiki/Virtue_Party" title="Virtue Party">Virtue Party</a> and then the AKP. Initially elected in the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_1994" title="Turkish local elections, 1994">1994 local elections</a>, he was re-elected in <a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_1999" title="Turkish local elections, 1999">1999</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_2004" title="Turkish local elections, 2004">2004</a> and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_2009" title="Turkish local elections, 2009">2009</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_local_elections,_2014" title="Turkish local elections, 2014">2014 local election</a>, Gökçek stood for a fifth term. The MHP metropolitan mayoral candidate for the 2009 local elections, conservative politician <a href="/wiki/Mansur_Yava%C5%9F" title="Mansur Yavaş">Mansur Yavaş</a>, stood as the CHP candidate against Gökçek. In a heavily controversial election, Gökçek was declared the winner by just 1% ahead of Yavaş amid allegations of systematic electoral fraud. With the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Electoral_Council_of_Turkey" title="Supreme Electoral Council of Turkey">Supreme Electoral Council</a> and courts rejecting Yavaş's appeals, he has declared intention to take the irregularities to the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Human_Rights" title="European Court of Human Rights">European Court of Human Rights</a>. Although Gökçek was inaugurated for a fifth term, most election observers believe<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> that Yavaş was the winner of the election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city suffered from a series of terrorist attacks in 2015 and 2016, most notably on <a href="/wiki/2015_Ankara_bombings" title="2015 Ankara bombings">10 October 2015</a>; <a href="/wiki/February_2016_Ankara_bombing" title="February 2016 Ankara bombing">17 February 2016</a>; <a href="/wiki/March_2016_Ankara_bombing" title="March 2016 Ankara bombing">13 March 2016</a>; and <a href="/wiki/2016_Turkish_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2016 Turkish coup d'état attempt">15 July 2016</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are about 50 museums in the city.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="An.C4.B1tkabir">Anıtkabir</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Anıtkabir">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/An%C4%B1tkabir" title="Anıtkabir">Anıtkabir</a> is located on an imposing hill, which forms the <i>Anıttepe</i> quarter of the city, where the mausoleum of <a href="/wiki/Mustafa_Kemal_Atat%C3%BCrk" title="Mustafa Kemal Atatürk">Mustafa Kemal Atatürk</a>, founder of the Republic of Turkey, stands. Completed in 1953, it is an impressive fusion of ancient and modern architectural styles. An adjacent museum houses a wax statue of Atatürk, his writings, letters and personal items, as well as an exhibition of photographs recording important moments in his life and during the establishment of the Republic. Anıtkabir is open every day, while the adjacent museum is open every day except Mondays.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:1010px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">

</div>

</div>
