<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angora_cat">Angora cat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Angora cat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Angora" title="Turkish Angora">Turkish Angora</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg/150px-Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg/225px-Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg/300px-Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Odd-eyed_Turkish_Angora_cat_-_20080830.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angora_cat" title="Angora cat">Angora cat</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ankara is home to a world-famous domestic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cat_breed" title="Cat breed">cat breed</a> – the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Angora" title="Turkish Angora">Turkish Angora</a>, called <i>Ankara kedisi</i> (Ankara cat) in Turkish. Turkish Angoras are one of the ancient, naturally occurring cat breeds, having originated in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia.</p>
<p>They mostly have a white, silky, medium to long length coat, no undercoat and a fine bone structure. There seems to be a connection between the Angora Cats and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persian_(cat)" title="Persian (cat)">Persians</a>, and the Turkish Angora is also a distant cousin of the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Van" title="Turkish Van">Turkish Van</a>. Although they are known for their shimmery white coat, currently there are more than twenty varieties including black, blue and reddish fur. They come in <a href="/wiki/Tabby_cat" title="Tabby cat">tabby</a> and tabby-white, along with smoke varieties, and are in every color other than pointed, lavender, and cinnamon (all of which would indicate breeding to an outcross.)</p>
<p>Eyes may be blue, green, or amber, or even one blue and one amber or green. The W gene which is responsible for the white coat and blue eye is closely related to the hearing ability, and the presence of a blue eye can indicate that the cat is deaf to the side the blue eye is located. However, a great many blue and <a href="/wiki/Odd-eyed_cat" title="Odd-eyed cat">odd-eyed</a> white cats have normal hearing, and even deaf cats lead a very normal life if kept indoors.</p>
<p>Ears are pointed and large, eyes are almond shaped and the head is massive with a two plane profile. Another characteristic is the tail, which is often kept parallel to the back.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angora_rabbit">Angora rabbit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Angora rabbit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbit</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2304" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg/150px-Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg/225px-Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg/300px-Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Joey_Giant_Angora_Buck.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbit</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Angora_rabbit" title="Angora rabbit">Angora rabbit</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <span lang="tr"><i>Ankara tavşanı</i></span>) is a variety of domestic rabbit bred for its long, soft hair. The Angora is one of the oldest types of domestic rabbit, originating in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia, along with the <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Angora" title="Turkish Angora">Angora cat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a>. The rabbits were popular pets with French royalty in the mid-18th century, and spread to other parts of Europe by the end of the century. They first appeared in the United States in the early 20th century. They are bred largely for their long <a href="/wiki/Angora_wool" title="Angora wool">Angora wool</a>, which may be removed by <a href="/wiki/Sheep_shearing" title="Sheep shearing">shearing</a>, combing, or <a href="/wiki/Plucking_(hair_removal)" title="Plucking (hair removal)">plucking</a> (gently pulling loose wool.)</p>
<p>Angoras are bred mainly for their wool because it is silky and soft. They have a humorous appearance, as they oddly resemble a fur ball. Most are calm and docile but should be handled carefully. Grooming is necessary to prevent the fiber from matting and felting on the rabbit. A condition called "wool block" is common in Angora rabbits and should be treated quickly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Sometimes they are shorn in the summer as the long fur can cause the rabbits to overheat.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Angora_goat">Angora goat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=55" title="Edit section: Angora goat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_angora_goat.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Quebec_angora_goat.jpg/150px-Quebec_angora_goat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Quebec_angora_goat.jpg/225px-Quebec_angora_goat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Quebec_angora_goat.jpg/300px-Quebec_angora_goat.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Quebec_angora_goat.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Angora_goat" title="Angora goat">Angora goat</a> (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a>: <span lang="tr"><i>Ankara keçisi</i></span>) is a breed of <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">domestic goat</a> that originated in Ankara and its surrounding region in central Anatolia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ekarius_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ekarius-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>This breed was first mentioned in the time of <a href="/wiki/Moses" title="Moses">Moses</a>, roughly in 1500 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The first Angora goats were brought to Europe by <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a>, about 1554, but, like later imports, were not very successful. Angora goats were first introduced in the United States in 1849 by Dr. James P. Davis. Seven adult goats were a gift from Sultan <a href="/wiki/Abd%C3%BClmecid_I" title="Abdülmecid I">Abdülmecid I</a> in appreciation for his services and advice on the raising of cotton.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Pile_(textile)" title="Pile (textile)">fleece</a> taken from an Angora goat is called <a href="/wiki/Mohair" title="Mohair">mohair</a>. A single goat produces between five and eight kilograms (11 and 18 <a href="/wiki/Pound_(mass)" title="Pound (mass)">pounds</a>) of hair per year. Angoras are shorn twice a year, unlike <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_sheep" title="Domestic sheep">sheep</a>, which are shorn only once. Angoras have high nutritional requirements due to their rapid hair growth. A poor quality diet will curtail mohair development. The United States, <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>, and South Africa are the top producers of mohair.</p>
<p>For a long period of time, Angora goats were bred for their white coat. In 1998, the Colored Angora Goat Breeders Association was set up to promote breeding of colored Angoras. Today, Angora goats produce white, black (deep black to greys and silver), red (the color fades significantly as the goat gets older), and brownish fiber.</p>
<p>Angora goats were depicted on the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">reverse</a> of the Turkish 50 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">lira</a> banknotes of 1938–1952.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=57" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Turkey" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Turkey">List of twin towns and sister cities in Turkey</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ankara&amp;action=edit&amp;section=58" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Ankara is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-40"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-40">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The citadel was depicted in the following Turkish banknotes:</span>
<ul>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">obverse</a> of the 1 <a href="/wiki/Turkish_lira" title="Turkish lira">lira</a> banknote of 1927–1939 (1. Emission Group – One Turkish Lira – <a class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E1/6.htm" rel="nofollow">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the obverse of the 5 lira banknote of 1927–1937 (1. Emission Group – Five Turkish Lira – <a class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E1/10.htm" rel="nofollow">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the <a href="/wiki/Obverse_and_reverse" title="Obverse and reverse">reverse</a> of the 10 lira banknote of 1927–1938 (1. Emission Group – Ten Turkish Lira – <a class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E1/14.htm" rel="nofollow">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the reverse of the 10 lira banknote of 1938–1952 (2. Emission Group – Ten Turkish Lira – <a class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E2/52.htm" rel="nofollow">I. Series</a>).</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">On the reverse of the 100 lira banknotes of 1983–1989 (7. Emission Group – One Hundred Turkish Lira – <a class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E7/256.htm" rel="nofollow">I. Series</a> &amp; <a class="external text" href="http://www.tcmb.gov.tr/yeni/banknote/E7/258.htm" rel="nofollow">II. Series</a>).</span></li>

<td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="2" style="padding:0.5em 0 0.3em; line-height:1.3em;">
<div><b>*</b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transcontinental_country" title="Transcontinental country">Transcontinental country</a>.<br/>
<b>†</b> See: <a href="/wiki/Positions_on_Jerusalem" title="Positions on Jerusalem">Positions on Jerusalem</a>. Both Israel and Palestinians claim Jerusalem as capital. <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> contains the Israeli parliament and almost all Israeli government ministries. <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> contains most foreign embassies in Israel; <a href="/wiki/Ramallah" title="Ramallah">Ramallah</a> is the administrative seat of the Palestinian Authority.<br/>
<b>+</b> According to the 1947 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Constitution of the Republic of China">Constitution of the Republic of China</a>, Nanjing is the official capital of the ROC, with Taipei as the <a href="/wiki/Temporary_capital" title="Temporary capital">seat of government</a>. See also <a href="/wiki/Political_status_of_Taiwan" title="Political status of Taiwan">Political status of Taiwan</a>.</div>
